Summary 165:
EU rules on advanced therapy medicinal products (OTM products)
EU policies on advanced therapies
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 726/2004 on the regulation of advanced therapy medicines
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down EU rules on the marketing and authorisation of advanced therapies* for the treatment of diseases and dysfunctions of the human body.
It aims to improve the quality of life of patients and improve the safety and effectiveness of these products.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all advanced therapies for diseases and disorders caused by the presence or absence of cells or tissues in the body. These include:
degenerative diseases, such as cancer;
cancer-related diseases, including inflammatory diseases, cardiovascular diseases, viral diseases, neurological disorders, viral infections and viral infections;
disease-related disorders, including viral infections, parasitic diseases, infectious diseases and viral diseases;
tuberculosis, tuberculosis-like diseases, viruses and parasitic diseases.
Manufacturing and marketing
Manufacturers must ensure that their products comply with the following requirements:
the products are manufactured and marketed in accordance with the EU’s national legislation on the manufacture and marketing of medicines;
they are accompanied by appropriate labelling, labelling and packaging;
the product design methods are described in a description of the physical characteristics and performance of the product and the product design.
The products must bear the following information on their packaging:
a description of their characteristics;
an indication of the active implantable medical device;
a product description of its characteristics and its design methods.
Labelling
The product must be accompanied by:
an explanation of the use of the device and its characteristics, if necessary with explanatory drawings and pictures;
information on the safety, efficacy and safety of the implantable device.
EU countries must ensure the labelling of the products and the package leaflet contains information on:
their safety and efficacy;
their duration of use;
any adverse events or reactions that may occur.
Evaluation procedure
The European Medicines Agency (EMA) must carry out a scientific evaluation of the medicinal product before authorising it to be marketed in the EU. It must:
assess the quality and non-clinical data submitted by small and medium-sized enterprises developing an advanced therapy product;
provide the Agency with all relevant quality and, where available, data required for scientific evaluation and certification;
certify that the product complies with the requirements laid down in Annex I to Directive 2001/83/EC on the manufacturing of medicinal products;
conduct a risk assessment and carry out an evaluation of its safety, effectiveness and safety profile.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2005.
BACKGROUND
The EU is a world leader in the field of biomedicine and has adopted a number of laws and regulations to encourage the development and use of innovative technologies. This regulation aims to ensure that these products are safe and effective.
For more information, see:
‘Advanced therapy medicines’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU) No 768/2004 of 21 December 2004 on the Regulation of the European Parliament and of the Council on the Authorisation of Advanced Therapy Medicines for the Treatment of Diseases and Dysfunctions (OJ L 183, 23.12.2004, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC, No 768) have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS
Commission Implementing Decision 2004/23/EC of 27 November 2004 establishing a European Committee for Advanced Therapies.

Summary 166:
EU type-approval system for motor vehicles and their trailers (EEC)
EU type–approval systems for motor vehicle and its trailers (EU)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2013 on type-approval of motor vehicles
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the type-approved vehicles and trailers of the European Union (EU).
It aims to reduce air pollution by emissions from motor vehicles.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
vehicles with a reference mass not exceeding 2.5 tonnes;
motor vehicles with a power rating of at least 3.5 kW;
hybrid vehicles* with at least 2 different energy converters and two different energy storage systems (on vehicle) for mass exceeding 2 840 kg and which meet the conditions laid down in this regulation and its implementing measures.
It does not apply to vehicles with direct injection engines.
Manufacturers’ obligations
Vehicle manufacturers must:
ensure that their vehicles comply with the requirements of the regulation;
make available to the European Commission, the European Agency for Safety and Health at European level, technical information on their vehicles’ emission control systems;
provide the Commission with information on the vehicle’s technical characteristics, including the type of engine and the number and type of exhaust system.
The Commission must review the regulation in the light of technological progress and assess its effectiveness.
Access to information
EU countries must ensure that vehicle manufacturers submit to the Commission information on:
the type of vehicle;
the number of exhaust systems and the total number of components and components in the vehicle.
Vehicles must also be made available to independent operators and authorised dealers and must be accompanied by training material.
Emissions/access to information must be submitted in a consistent manner, initially in accordance with the technical requirements of OASIS format. The Commission must monitor the quality of the information submitted and ensure that it complies with the regulation.
In addition, vehicle manufacturers must provide the Commission and the European Parliament with technical information concerning:
roadworthiness of vehicles;
compulsory maintenance and repair of vehicle systems and components;
vehicle emissions and access to information;
access to vehicle repair and maintenance information.
National authorities must also ensure that vehicles are registered and registered in their respective EU countries.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATING DIRECTIVE APPLY?

It applies from 2 January 2013. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 2 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a number of measures to tackle air pollution caused by motor vehicles, including:
measures to improve the safety of drivers and passengers;
measures against the harmful effects of climate change.
For more information, see:
‘Emissions’ (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC), Euratom, 2.1.2013, pp. 1-5
Successive amendments to Regulation (E) No 1 have been incorporated into the original document. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 167:
EU rules on the authorisation of food substances
EU rules governing the authorisations of foods
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 178/2002 establishing a Community list of authorised substances
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a common procedure for the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) to authorise food substances.
It aims to ensure that the EU’s food safety rules are applied uniformly throughout the EU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries’ sectoral food laws. It does not apply to:
the food sector;
the agricultural sector; or
the aquaculture sector.
Authorisations
The European Commission publishes a list of the authorised substances in force in the EU, known as the ‘EU list’. The list is updated every 2 years.
The EU list is maintained by the Commission. It is updated by the EFSA, which publishes the list on its website.
EU countries must inform the European Commission of the names of the substances on the list and the reasons for their inclusion in the list. The Commission publishes the EU list on the basis of a risk assessment carried out in accordance with Regulation (EU) No 596/2013 on food safety.
Risk assessment
The Commission must carry out risk assessments every 3 years. The results of these assessments must be published in the Official Journal of the European Union (OJEU). The Commission must publish a report on the results of the risk assessment every 5 years. This report must be made available to the public and to the European Parliament, the European Council and the European Economic and Social Committee on Food Safety and Health.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
The Regulation entered into force on 20 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
The EFSA is responsible for the safety of food and the protection of human health and the environment. Its role is to ensure a high level of protection of the health and safety of human life and health of consumers.
For more information, see:
Food safety: EU rules on authorised substances (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Authorised substance: a substance which is authorised to be used in the manufacture, transport or storage of foodstuffs.
ACT
Commission Regulation (Euratom) No 184/2008 of 20 January 2008 establishing a common list of substances authorised in the field of food.
REFERENCES

Summary 168:
EU rules on accreditation, market surveillance, controls of products from non-EU countries and the CE marking (until 31 December 2020)
EU rules in the field of accreditation and market surveillance: accreditation of conformity assessment bodies performing conformity assessment activities
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2008 — accreditation requirements for conformity assessment* bodies
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes rules on the organisation and operation of the European Union (EU) accreditation* bodies* that perform conformity assessment (CE) activities.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the following sectors: drug precursors, medical devices, medicinal products for human and veterinary use, motor vehicles and aviation.
It does not apply to:
medical devices;
motor vehicles;
personal protective equipment;
pharmaceutical products;
electrical products.
Objectives
The aim of the regulation is to ensure that EU countries’ national accreditation bodies:
ensure that products which are subject to CE conformity assessment have the necessary documentation and information to demonstrate that they meet the necessary requirements;
establish a system for the exchange of information on products presenting a risk;
monitor and exchange of test reports and certificates between national accreditations bodies;
assist the European Commission in its activities;
ensuring that the CE CE marking is affixed on products which present a risk.
The European Commission:
provides the Commission with information on the products and their conformity assessment results;
is assisted by the European Rapid Information System (ANNEXEX);
ensures that the Commission has access to the information it needs to carry out its tasks;
coordinates with EU countries and other EU countries on products presented as a risk to the EU’s internal market.
Rules on market surveillance
EU countries must cooperate, at national level, with national market surveillance authorities and exchange information with them relating to products which they suspect present a threat.
National authorities must:
assess whether a product presents a risk,
identify the risks,
monitor the results of testing carried out,
take provisional restrictive measures taken,
make contact with the economic operators concerned and
take the necessary samples of products to establish whether the product meets the necessary conditions for its use;
investigate and prosecute infringements of EU rules on CE marking;
take appropriate measures to prevent the use of products which do not meet the requirements of this regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The EU accreditation regulation has applied since 1 December 2008.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
European accreditation (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Conformity assessment body: a body that carries out conformity assessment tests on a product to assess whether it meets the essential requirements of EU law.
* CE marking: a CE marking affixed by the manufacturer or his authorised representative to a product which is intended to be used only for the purpose of ensuring that the product complies with EU legislation.
ACT
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 550/2008 of 21 December 2008 laying down rules for the organisation, operation and recognition of the accreditation organisations of conformity assessments bodies performing CE assessment activities (OJ L 183, 21.12.2008, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments and corrections to Regulation (Euratom), Euratom have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 169:
EU-Iceland agreement on the execution of arrest warrants for the arrest and extradition of suspects
EU–Iceland Agreement
SUMMARY OF:
Agreement between the European Union and its Member States, the Kingdom of Norway and the Republic of Iceland on the arrest warrant for the execution and subsequent extradition of persons suspected of serious crimes
Decision (EU) 2017/852 concluding the agreement between the EU and its member countries, the EU countries, Iceland and Norway
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND OF THE DECISION?
The agreement aims to facilitate the execution, on behalf of the EU, of an arrest warrant issued by an EU country against a person suspected of committing a serious crime.
The decision to execute the warrant must be taken within 30 days of receiving the request. The decision may be taken no later than 30 days after receipt of the request, unless the request is accompanied by a request for the person’s surrender or subsequent extradition.
In the event of multiple requests, the decision must be made within 15 days of receipt of all the requests. It may be extended by a further 30 days if there are multiple requests or if there is a dispute between the issuing and executing countries.
It does not apply to:
the arrest warrant itself;
the execution of an extradition request; or the subsequent extradition request.
KEY POINTS
Arrest warrant
An arrest warrant:
is issued by the issuing country on the basis of a request from the country in which it was issued;
is valid for a period of 5 years;
it is valid for 5 years.
An executing the warrant;
may be executed by the country which issued it.
the executing country may refuse to execute it if it considers that the person is not a threat to public order or the security of the country concerned.
If the executing country considers that a person is a risk to the public order, it may refuse execution of the warrant. The executing country must inform the person and inform them of the reasons for its decision. The person may have the right to legal counsel.
When an executing country refuses to execute a warrant, the person may appeal against the decision.
A decision may also be refused if:
there are grounds for non-execution;
there is no reason to believe that the warrant is valid;
an executing country does not have jurisdiction over the case;
a person has not been informed of the reason for the decision;
they have not been given the opportunity to challenge the decision in court.
EU countries may decide to suspend or withdraw an execution of a warrant if they consider that it is not valid.
Extradition request
An extradition request may be sent to the country where the person has been arrested. It must be accompanied by:
a copy of the original arrest warrant,
a description of the nature and duration of the offence and the grounds for its execution;
information on the person concerned, including the nature of the crime and the circumstances in which the person was arrested;
any other relevant information requested by the requesting country.
Where the country that issued the warrant does not comply with the conditions laid down in the warrant, it must return the person to its country of origin.
Expiry of an execution warrant
The executing country has 30 days from the date on which it received the request to decide whether to execute or not to issue the warrant to the person who is the subject of the extradition request, including:
whether or not the warrant has been executed;
whether the person in question has been convicted of a crime punishable by imprisonment;
where the executing judicial authority has surrendered the person;
if the executing court has given its consent to the extradition;
when the executing judge has been appointed by a country which has surrendered a person.
FROM WHEN DO THE DECISIONS ENTER INTO FORCE?
   
The agreements entered into force on 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
 
  The EU is a party to the Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court (ICC).
The EU is one of 3 contracting parties to the agreement. The other 2 are the EU Member States of the European Economic Area (EEA).
KEY TERMS
* Arrest warrant: a warrant issued to arrest a person for the purpose of preventing, investigating or prosecuting a criminal offence.
* Extradition: a request to extradite a person to another country for the purposes of preventing or prosecuting that offence. The term ‘extradition’ is used in the agreement to refer to the transfer of a person from one country to another.
REFERENCES
Act
Entry into force
Deadline for transposition in the Member States
Official Journal
Council Decision (EU, Euratom) 2017-852
1.1.2018

OJ L 136, 1.1-2.2018, pp. 1-2

Summary 170:
Consumers’ rights on rail transport
Consumers' rights on railway transport
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2006 — uniform rules for the carriage of passengers on rail passenger services
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
 
   
It sets out uniform rules on the carriage charge* and carriage charge*, as well as the information to be provided to passengers.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
all passenger services on the European Union’s (EU) railway network;
urban, suburban and regional passenger services.
It does not apply to the following:
the carriage of goods by road;
traffic management;
passenger information;
access to services;
ticketing information.
Passengers may submit a complaint to any railway undertaking involved.
Complaints must be made to the competent authorities of the EU country in which the railway service is operated.
The rules apply to all passengers, irrespective of whether they are:
traveling by road or by rail;
using public transport;
paying a carriage charge; or
paying for a ticket.
EU countries may grant exemptions from the application of the regulation to certain types of passenger services, such as:
railway passenger services operated by a private company;
railways operated by the European Commission;
busy-busy passenger services; and
the passenger information system.
In addition, the regulation provides for:
information to disabled and persons with reduced mobility;
travelers’ information on the conditions of carriage;
information on the charges;
the conditions under which the ticket is valid;
conditions for the refund of carriage charges.
Exemption from liability
The European Commission may grant an exemption from liability for loss or damage arising from the fact that the passenger does not conform to the formalities required by customs or other administrative authorities.
Liability of the carrier
The carrier is not liable to the passenger for loss, damage or loss arising from:
failure to comply with the conditions and limitations laid down in the regulation;
loss or damage resulting from the failure of the passenger to conform with the requirements of customs or administrative authorities;
non-compliance with the rules laid down by the Commission.
Where the carrier is liable, it may be brought against the passenger only subject to the conditions set out in these uniform rules.
Penalties for infringements of the rules are effective, proportionate and dissuasive. They must be effective and proportionate, and must not be dissuasive in the light of the seriousness of the infringements.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2007. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
The EU has a high level of consumer protection in the field of transport. This regulation is part of a package of measures designed to improve the quality of transport services in the EU.
For more information, see:
‘Railway consumer protection’ on the Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Carriage charge: a charge charged on the basis of the number of seats available on a train, the number or type of carriage, the distance between the carriage and the destination, the duration of the journey and the price of the ticket. The carriage charge is calculated according to the number and type of seat available on the train. It is calculated in accordance with the EU rules on carriage charge.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 550/2006 of 21 December 2006 on the application, on behalf of the European Community, of the uniform rules concerning the carriage charges and carriage charges applicable to passenger services (OJ L 304, 1.12.2006, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (Euratom) no 550/06 have been incorporated into the original document. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
last update 14.02.2016



Summary 171:
Harmonised data on vocational education and training statistics
Harmonomically harmonised data in the field
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 852/2005 on harmonised European Union (EU) statistics on the quality of vocational education
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes common statistical standards that permit the production of harmonised EU-wide data for vocational education (VET) and training (EU-SILC) statistics.
It aims to improve the quality and reliability of these statistics, thus contributing to the implementation of the Lisbon strategy.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries’ national authorities and the European Commission (Eurostat).
EU countries must collect and transmit data on:
the quality of VETs;
the number of students in each EU country;
participation in vocational education;
quality of training;
access to vocational education.
The data must be collected and transmitted to Eurostat by:
national authorities and Eurostat;
Eurostat; and
the European Union Agency for Fundamental Rights and Citizenship.
Data and metadata
Data must be supplied annually, if not otherwise specified, within the deadlines agreed between Eurostat and the national authorities taking into account the latest agreements between the UIS, the OECD and the Commission.
They must be transmitted in accordance with the following rules:
data and metadata must be provided in the form set out in the annex to the regulation;
they must contain:
a description of the subject of the data;
a summary of the results of the survey;
data on the number and duration of students and the number of teachers and vocational education providers;
information on the types of courses offered and the duration of the courses;
annexes to the data collection and the transmission of data subject to statistical confidentiality.
National authorities must:
ensure that the data are collected in a language easily understood by the general public;
provide the Commission with a list of data sources;
use administrative data sources to reduce the burden on respondents;
assist Eurostat in the collection and processing of data and metadata;
make use of the information provided by national authorities, Eurostat, the United Nations Institute for Statistics (UNIS) and the OECD;
collect, analyse and transmit the data collected by Eurostat to the European Statistical Office of the European Communities (ESO).
Data collection
The European Commission must collect, analyse, process and transmit VET data in line with the requirements laid down in Annexes 1 and 2 of the regulation. It must also collect and analyse the data it receives from national authorities.
Reporting
The Commission must report to the Council every 3 years on the results obtained from the VET and on the progress made.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2006.
BACKGROUND
The Lisbon strategy is a key element in developing and promoting a skilled, trained and adaptable workforce. It is one of the pillars of the EU’s strategic objectives.
For more information, see:
Lifelong learning (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Vocational education: vocational training is a form of lifelong learning that is designed to develop and promote lifelong learning skills.
* VET: vocational education is a type of training that is aimed at lifelong learning.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (Euratom) No 802/2005/EC of 22 and 23 March 2005 on the harmonisation of European Union statistics concerning the quality, scope, reliability and availability of Vocational Education and Training statistics (recast) (Codified version) (OJ L 31, 23.3.2005, pp. 1-2)

Summary 172:
EU energy statistics: renewable energy and energy from waste (REFERENCES
EU energy data
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2008 — renewable energy statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the reporting of renewable energy (RE) statistics and final energy consumption statistics.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to the EU’s energy sector.
It covers:
energy production and consumption;
energy from waste;
renewable energy statistics and energy consumption.
EU countries must report to the European Commission every 2 years on the renewable energy they produce and the energy they consume, as well as on the total amount of renewable and energy-from-waste they generate.
The data must cover:
gross electricity and heat production;
gross energy consumption; and
total renewable energy production.
Data must be collected and transmitted to the Commission by:
the EU countries’ national authorities;
the European Atomic Energy Community (Euratom);
the EEA countries and the European Maritime and Fisheries Agency (EMSA).
The Commission must transmit the data to the EEA by 30 November of the year following the reported period. The data must be transmitted in accordance with the following deadlines:

Regulations (EU) 2021/2023 amending Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 605/2013 and (EU 2020/2024) amending the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMESSAGE APPLACE?
The regulations apply from 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a number of measures to improve the quality of EU energy statistics. These include:
EU-wide renewable energy targets (see summary);
EU rules on renewable energy efficiency;
EU standards on energy efficiency.
For more information, see:
‘EU renewable energy’ on the Euratom website.
* KEY TERMS

Summary 173:
Disabled passengers’ rights on the transport of persons with reduced mobility on the European Union’s public transport system
Disabled persons’ right on the transportation system
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2004 on the rights of passengers on the carriage of persons in wheelchairs and mobility devices
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that passengers travelling on public transport have the same rights as other passengers.
It sets out rules on:
the carriage of passengers by road and by rail;
the provision of assistance to passengers;
access to services;
information on the conditions of the service.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
bus and coach passengers, irrespective of their physical or mental disability;
passengers on board buses and coaches, regardless of their mobility devices;
travelers on board trains and on board coaches.
Passengers have the following rights:
to be provided with information before and during the journey;
to receive assistance free of charge;
in the event of an accident arising out of the use of the bus or coach, the carrier must provide reasonable and proportionate assistance with regard to the passengers' immediate practical needs following the accident.
The legislation does not apply to passengers who are:
deafened or physically unable to hear or see;
visually impaired;
impaired or partially sighted;
disabled persons;
persons who cannot walk or use a wheelchairs or mobility devices.
those who are unable to use a wheelchair;
people who have reduced mobility.
EU countries must ensure that:
transport services are provided in a safe and operationally feasible manner;
there is no discrimination based on the disability of the person;
services are provided for in accordance with the rules of the European Commission;
all passengers are entitled to the same information as the general public, including:
information regarding the service;
an estimate of the estimated departure time;
a description of the number of seats available on the bus and coach;
any other information that may be necessary for the safety and operation of the services.
In addition, EU countries must:
ensure that the information provided by the carrier is:
informal;
clear and understandable;
accessible;
free of charge.
Directive (EU) 2019/849 on the accessibility of services for persons with disabilities (see summary)
The directive repeals Directive 2004/36/EC and its subsequent amendments.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
  The regulation applies from 1 January 2005. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2006.
BACKGROUND
   
 
For more information, see:
‘Access to transport’ (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Wheelchair passenger: a person who is physically or mentally disabled and has reduced mobility and who is dependent on a mobility device.
* Train passenger: any person who uses a wheelchair or mobility device to travel by road or by train.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 			
	
Commission Implementing Decision 2004/96/EC of 21 December 2004 on the right of passengers to travel on the road and on the coach of the Member States and repealing Directive 2003/37/EC.
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC), as amended by Directive 2014/13/EU, have been incorporated into the original document. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 174:
EU aquaculture statistics
EU aquaiculture statistics
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 788/96 — EU aqua-fishery statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the collection and transmission of EU aquaquaculture data to the European Union (EU).
It aims to improve the quality of the EU’s fisheries statistics.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
the production of fish and molluscs in freshwater and saltwater on EU Member States’ territory;
the activities of hatcheries and nurseries;
production of aquatic animals in nurseries.
It does not apply to the production of live fish and crustaceans.
The purpose of the regulation is to provide the European Commission with reliable, comparable, comparable and comparable data on the production by species of fish, mollusk species and aquatic animals for fishery statistics purposes.
EU Member States must:
identify the number of species and quantities of fish they produce;
provide a description of the methods and methods of production;
report to the Commission on the data they have collected and the results they have provided.
Reporting
The Commission must publish a report on the results of the reporting every 3 years.
Each Member State must submit a report to the EU Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee on the quality and quantity of the data it has collected. The report must include:
a description of aquacultural activities;
an estimate of the total production; and
a list of the species and the quantities of species produced.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULE APPLACE IN FORCE?
 
   
It has applied since 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a common fisheries policy for aquiculture.
For more information, see:
‘Aquaculture’ on the Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU) No 768/96/2008 of 21 December 2008 on the collection, transmission and dissemination of Community statistics relating to aqua‐fishing activities conducted in the Member States

Summary 175:
Convention on the conservation and management of fishery resources in the North-East Atlantic Fisheries Commission (NEEFCC)
Convention upon the conclusion of the Convention on the Conservation and Management of Fishery Resources
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated act (EU) 2017/852 on the implementation of Articles 24 and 25 of the NEEFFC Convention
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION AND THE REGULATION?
The decision aims to establish a framework for multilateral cooperation between the European Community (now the EU) and its Member States to ensure the conservation, management and sustainable use of fisheries in the north-east Atlantic fisheries area defined by the Convention (the Convention Area).
KEY POINTS
The convention provides for the establishment of a regulatory area to be managed by the European Union (EU).
The regulation sets out detailed rules for the notification and authorisation of the fishery resource to be notified, procedures for prior notification of entry into port and for the cancellation of authorisations, as well as for the authorisation to land or tranship.
In addition, the regulation establishes contact points for receiving notifications and issuing authorisations in accordance with the convention’s rules.
National authorities must notify the Commission and the European Economic and Social Committee (EASC) of the EU Member States of the lists of the fishing resources to which the regulation applies. These must be available 24 hours a day.
Member States must report to the Commission or the body designated by it any infringements of the conservation or management measures adopted by NEAFCFFC. These infringements must be reported to the following an inspection. The Commission or body must promptly inform the body of the infringements and follow-up of infringements.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DECISION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2017.
BACKGROUND
The Convention provides for an appropriate framework to ensure multilateral conservation and managed fisheries.
The EU is a contracting party to the convention.
For more information, see:
‘Convention Area’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision No 852/2016/EU of 21 December 2016 on the application of Articles 25 and 24 of the convention relating to the notification, authorisation and conservation measures adopted in the Convention Area (OJ L 347, 28.12.2016, pp. 1-8)
RELATED DOCUMENTS
Council Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2017-852 of 27 November 2017 on the enforcement of the rules of the regulation relating to fishery management in the convention area and repealing Council Regulation (EC) No 596/2006 (OJC) No 652/2006.
Regulation (EC), Euratom No 653/2006 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 11 December 2006 on the protection of the marine environment in the area defined in Article 25 of Article 24 and 26 of the Convention Area (Codified version).

Summary 176:
EU Ecolabel — rules on the labelling of foodstuffs
European Ecolabelling: rules for the use of organic products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1980/2000 on the use, labelling and certification of food and feed products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a European Union (EU) ecolabel (ecolabel) scheme.
It aims to ensure that products labelled with an organic label are sold in the EU without any confusion for consumers.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all food and food-related products, including food, feed and feed additives.
Products certified as organic would be eligible for award of the EU EColabel, as long as they comply with the relevant product group criteria and do not present a risk to human health or the environment.
Eligible products
Products that are not organic must be labelled as such, unless they meet the following criteria:
they do not contain substances that are harmful to human or animal health or to the environment;
they are not intended for human consumption.
Organic products must bear the following information:
the name of the producer;
the product’s provenance;
a description of the products’ composition and characteristics;
an indication of the quality of the product;
their presence or absence in the food chain.
The EU EcolABelling Board (EUEB) is the body responsible for administering the scheme. It is chaired by the European Commission and is composed of representatives of the Member States and the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA).
The European Commission is assisted by a Committee.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
The Regulation entered into force on 1 July 2000.
BACKGROUND
 
 Â  Â
 			
For more information, see:
‘Ecolabel’ (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Organic products: products that are produced from organic ingredients and which are certified as such.
* Food and feed additive: products which are intended to be used as additives or preservatives in food or feed, and which contain substances or ingredients that are intended for use as preservatives.
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 177:
Supplementary protection certificate for medicinal products
Supplemental protection certificate
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1901/2006 — supplementary protection certificate relating to a medicinal product for which marketing authorisation has been granted
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a system for the granting of supplementary protection certificates (SPCs) to the holder of a national or European patent relating to medicinal products.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EU) No 2001/83/EC (see summary).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
any medicinal product protected by a valid basic patent and for which the first authorisation to place it on the market as a pharmaceutical product was obtained in Malta prior to 1 May 2004;
any pharmaceutical product which has been placed on the EU market since 1 July 2002 and which was granted a certificate.
The SPCs are valid for 5 years from the date on which they are granted. The duration of the certificate may not exceed 5 years.
Application for a certificate
An application for a SPC must be submitted by the holder to the competent authority of the EU country in which it is issued. The application must include:
the name and address of the holder;
the nature and nature of the product covered by the SPC;
a description of the medicinal product;
an indication of the annual fee to be paid for the extension of the duration.
If an application for an extended duration is pending, the applicant must include the particulars referred to in Article 7(3 of the regulation.
An extension of a certificate may be made within 6 months of the expiry of the original SPC.
A certificate may expire at the end of the 5-year period if the holder surrenders it or if it is not paid in time.
Expiry
The certificate may lapse:
at the end the period provided for in Article 13;
if the certificate holder gives up the certificate or if the product no longer meets the conditions for its use; or
if it is withdrawn from the market following withdrawal of the appropriate authorisation or authorisations.
Invalidity of the validity
The holder may submit an application to the body responsible under national law for the revocation of the corresponding basic patent.

Summary 178:
Convention on jurisdiction in civil and commercial matters in the European Union (EU) (Lugano Convention)
Convention of the European Parliament and of the Council of 26 February 2000 on jurisdiction and enforcement in civil matters in civil, commercial and commercial disputes
SUMMARY OF:
Conventions on jurisdiction, enforcement and enforcement of judgments in civil or commercial matters
Decision (EC) No 552/2004 on the conclusion of the Convention on jurisdiction applicable to nationals of the Member States of the Community of the Swiss Confederation (Lagano Convention).
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE CONVENTION AND THE DECISION?
The convention establishes a legal framework for the application of the rules of law applicable to EU nationals in respect of the jurisdiction of the courts and tribunals of the contracting parties.
The decision concludes the convention on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
The parties to the convention are:
non-EU nationals who are not nationals of a Member State bound by the Convention in which they are domiciled;
citizens of the States bound by this convention who are governed by the rules applicable to the nationals of that State.
In civil matters, the convention applies to the following:
the judgment of the court or tribunal in which the proceedings are held;
the decision of the Court of Justice of the Federal Republic of Switzerland;
a judgment issued by a court in the territory of an EU country;
an agreement between the parties to a commercial or commercial dispute.
Where the parties have not been able to present their case before a court, the judgment is enforceable only in the Member State in which has jurisdiction over the case, i.e. the country in which it was entered.
A party may not contest the jurisdiction or enforcement of a judgment.
If the parties do not appear before an appellate court in proceedings concerning an appeal brought by the applicant, they may not enforce the judgment. This rule does not apply where appearance was entered to contest jurisdiction, or where another court has exclusive jurisdiction by virtue of Article 22.3 of the convention.
Annexes V and VI to the Convention provide for translations into their languages. The annexes also provide for the exchange of information on judgments and court settlements.
When enforcement is sought, the parties must comply with the convention’s rules on enforcement and enforceability. The parties must:
be informed of the nature of the judgment;
notify the court which delivered the judgment/approved the court settlement;
be accompanied by a translation into English and French.
Appeals must be brought before the courts of the country where the judgment or court settlement was delivered;
appear before the court of jurisdiction in the case of an appeal;
have the right to appeal against the judgment and/or court settlement.
Exemption from enforcement
The judgment and court settlement may not be enforced in cases where the parties are not the same country.
Jurisdiction
Where enforcement is not applicable, the party against whom enforcement is requested is not a national of the party to which enforcement is being sought.
Enforcement may be granted only where the party is a resident of the State where enforcement is to be carried out. The law of the state in which enforcement takes place is applicable. If enforcement is carried out, the law of that state is applicable to all the parties, including the parties who are the subject of enforcement proceedings.
Implementation
The contracting parties must apply the rules laid down in Annexes V through VI and VIII to this convention in order to:
ensure that judgments and decisions are enforced in accordance with the provisions of this convention;
apply the rules set out in the annexes;
take the necessary measures to ensure that enforcement is effective and enforceable;
implement the rules and procedures laid down by the convention in line with its annexes.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The Convention entered into force on 1 July 2004.
BACKGROUND
   
 
The Lugano Convention is one of a number of legal instruments designed to protect the rights and interests of EU citizens against fraud and abuse of power.
For more information, see:
‘Judges’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision 2004/552/EC of 27 February 2004 concerning the conclusion in favour of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland (OJ L 347, 28.3.2004, pp. 1-8)
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 696/2004 of 27 June 2004 on the application by the Member states of the Treaty on the Functioning of the Union of the Schengen Economic Area of the International Convention on Jurisdiction and Enforcement of Judgments in Civil and Commercial Matters (Luxembourg Convention) and repealing Protocol 2 of Protocol 2.1.2004.
Successive amendments to the Treaty have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version
